<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The aggregate market value of common stock held by non-affiliates of the registrant was approximately $6,100,000 based on its closing price per share of $6.45 on March 31, 2015. On March 31, 2015, there were 4,028,951 shares of common stock outstanding. No officer or director beneficially held shares of the Company&#146;s Common Stock as of December 3, 2015. Shareholders who owned 5 percent or more of the outstanding common stock at that time have been excluded in that such persons may be deemed affiliates. The determination of affiliate status is not necessarily a conclusive determination for other purposes.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">2015 ANNUAL REPORT ON FORM&nbsp;10-K</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">PART&nbsp;I</font></b><a name="PARTI_042000"></a></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Disclosure Regarding Forward-Looking Statements</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K contains, and our periodic filings with the Securities and Exchange Commission (the &#147;SEC&#148;) and written and oral statements made by the Company&#146;s sole officer and director to press, potential investors, securities analysts and others, will contain, forward-looking statements within the meaning of Section&nbsp;27A of the Securities Act of 1933 (the &#147;Securities Act&#148;) and Section&nbsp;21E of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934 (the &#147;Exchange Act&#148;), and the Company intends that such forward-looking statements be subject to the safe harbors created thereby. These forward-looking statements are not historical facts, but rather are predictions and generally can be identified by use of statements that include phrases such as &#147;believe,&#148; &#147;expect,&#148; &#147;anticipate,&#148; &#147;estimate,&#148; &#147;intend,&#148; &#147;plan,&#148; &#147;foresee,&#148; &#147;looking ahead,&#148; &#147;is confident,&#148; &#147;should be,&#148; &#147;will,&#148; &#147;predicted,&#148; &#147;likely&#148; or other words or phrases of similar import. Similarly, statements that describe or contain information related to matters such as our intent, belief, or expectation with respect to financial performance, claims resolution under the Plan (as defined below), cash availability and cost-cutting measures are forward-looking statements. These forward-looking statements often reflect a number of assumptions and involve known and unknown risks, uncertainties and other factors that could cause our actual results to differ materially from those currently anticipated in these forward-looking statements. In light of these risks and uncertainties, the forward-looking events might or might not occur, which may affect the accuracy of forward-looking statements and cause the actual results of the Company to be materially different from any future results expressed or implied by such forward-looking statements.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In this Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K, references to &#147;the Company,&#148; &#147;Comdisco Holding,&#148; &#147;we,&#148; &#147;us&#148; and &#147;our&#148; mean Comdisco Holding Company,&nbsp;Inc., its consolidated subsidiaries, including Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc., Comdisco Ventures Fund A, LLC (formerly Comdisco Ventures,&nbsp;Inc.) and its predecessors, except in each case where the context indicates otherwise. References to &#147;Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc.&#148; mean Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc. and its subsidiaries, prior to the Company&#146;s emergence from bankruptcy on August&nbsp;12, 2002, except where the context indicates otherwise.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Important factors that could cause actual results to differ materially from those suggested by these written or oral forward-looking statements, and that could adversely affect our future financial performance, include the risk factors discussed in Item 1A, &#147;Risk Factors&#148;. Many of the risk factors that could affect the results of the Company&#146;s operations are beyond our ability to control or predict.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Available Information</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company&#146;s website address is www.comdisco.com. The Company makes available through its website its Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K, Quarterly Reports on Form&nbsp;10-Q, Current Reports on Form&nbsp;8-K and all amendments to those reports, as soon as reasonably practicable after such material is electronically filed with the SEC. The Company also makes available through the website its press releases, the Code of Conduct Applicable to its Chief Executive Officer and Authorized Representatives, the Employee Code of Conduct, the Audit Committee Charter, the Disclosure Controls Committee Charter and the Compensation Committee Charter, as well as contact information for the Audit Committee. Information contained on the Company&#146;s website is not intended to be part of this Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">ITEM 1. BUSINESS</font></b><a name="ITEM1_BUSINESS_042005"></a></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company emerged from Chapter 11 bankruptcy proceedings on August&nbsp;12, 2002. The purpose of the Company is to sell, collect or otherwise reduce to money in an orderly manner the remaining assets of the corporation. Pursuant to the Company&#146;s First Amended Joint Plan of Reorganization (the &#147;Plan&#148;) and restrictions contained in the Company&#146;s Certificate of Incorporation (the &#147;Certificate&#148;), the Company is specifically prohibited from engaging in any business activities inconsistent with its limited business purpose.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company filed, on August&nbsp;12, 2004, a Certificate of Dissolution with the Secretary of State of the State of Delaware to formally extinguish Comdisco Holding Company,&nbsp;Inc.&#146;s corporate existence with the State of Delaware except for the purpose of completing the wind down contemplated by the Plan.&#160; Capitalized terms used but not defined in the Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K have the meanings as defined in the Plan.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">1<a name="PB_1_152657_7056"></a></p>
<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade align="left" style="color:#010101;"></div>
</div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;"><a href="#TableOfContents" title="Click to go to Table of Contents">Table of Contents</a></font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Under the Plan, the Company was charged with, and has been, liquidating its assets. While there have been no changes either to the Plan, or the Company&#146;s obligations under it, the Company adopted ASU 2013-07, <i>Liquidation Basis of Accounting </i>as of October&nbsp;1, 2014 and accordingly determined that liquidation was imminent. Therefore, effective October&nbsp;1, 2014, the Company applied the liquidation basis&nbsp;of accounting on a prospective basis. </font>The liquidation basis of accounting requires the Company to estimate net cash flows from operations and to accrue all costs associated with implementing and completing the plan of liquidation and requires management to make estimates that affect the amounts reported in the consolidated financial statements and the related notes. &#160;Due to the adoption of the liquidation basis of accounting as of October&nbsp;1, 2014, the comparability of results of operations of current year periods to prior year periods is limited.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company is currently projecting December&nbsp;31, 2016 as the end date for its wind down of operations. It is anticipated that by this date the Company will have, among other things: finalized the settlement of the SIP, received the projected escrow funds from the Ebates transaction, reduced all of its assets to cash, resolved its final federal and state tax obligations, determined its final CDR liability (which will include the impact of the actual distribution by the Litigation Trust to the C-4 creditors), made distributions of all available cash to holders of its common stock and CDRs in the manner and priorities set forth in the Plan, cancelled such common stock and CDRs and completed all regulatory filings.&#160; Accordingly, it has made appropriate expense accruals for such time period in its calculation of Net Assets in Liquidation. However, the projected remaining wind down period could be either shortened or lengthened by other intervening matters not currently known to management.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">General Development of Business</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Comdisco Holding Company,&nbsp;Inc. was formed on August&nbsp;8, 2002 for the purpose of selling, collecting or otherwise reducing to money in an orderly manner the remaining assets of the Company and all of its direct and indirect subsidiaries, including Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc. The Company&#146;s business purpose is limited to the orderly sale or run-off of all its remaining assets. Pursuant to the Plan and restrictions contained in its Certificate, the Company is specifically prohibited from engaging in any business activities inconsistent with its limited business purpose.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Since emerging from bankruptcy proceedings on August&nbsp;12, 2002 (See Reorganized Corporate History), the Company has, pursuant to the Plan, focused on the monetization of its remaining assets and the wind down of operations, including, reducing organizational size, distributions to creditors, resolution of outstanding litigation and claims, the settlement of any tax obligations to various taxing authorities and jurisdictions, and the liquidation of legal entities of the Company.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company expects net cash provided by operating activities to continue to decrease until the completion of the wind down of its operations. &#160;The Company also expects operating expenses to continue as it pursues its business purpose under the Plan.&#160; Therefore, comparisons of quarter-to-quarter or year-to-year results of operations should not be relied upon as an indication of the Company&#146;s future performance.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company has reduced the size and complexity of its organizational and systems infrastructure concurrently with the monetization of its assets. During 2008, the Company received permission to begin the process of abandoning and destroying certain of its stored paper and electronic records for periods prior to January&nbsp;1, 1997.&#160; As of the date of this filing, the Company destroyed substantially all of those records.&#160; As of December&nbsp;3, 2015, the Company had a total of five employees (one full-time and four part-time), a decrease of approximately 99 percent from approximately 600 employees upon emergence from bankruptcy proceedings on August&nbsp;12, 2002. Three to four consultants periodically assist the Company on a consulting basis.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On August&nbsp;12, 2004, Randolph I. Thornton&#146;s appointment as Initial Disbursing Agent became effective. As Initial Disbursing Agent, Mr.&nbsp;Thornton performs the roles and responsibilities of the Board of Directors and officers of the Company, including all measures that are necessary to complete the administration of the reorganized debtors&#146; Plan and Chapter 11 cases. Mr.&nbsp;Thornton serves as Chief Executive Officer, President and Secretary and is the sole director and executive officer of the Company.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">2<a name="PB_2_152715_5335"></a></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;"><a href="#TableOfContents" title="Click to go to Table of Contents">Table of Contents</a></font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Reorganized Corporate History</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On July&nbsp;16, 2001, Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc. and fifty of its domestic subsidiaries filed voluntary petitions for relief under Chapter 11 of the United States Bankruptcy Code in the United States Bankruptcy court for the Northern District of Illinois Eastern Division (the &#147;Bankruptcy court&#148;) (consolidated case number 01-24795). Comdisco Holding Company,&nbsp;Inc., as the successor company to Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc., emerged from bankruptcy under the Plan that became effective on August&nbsp;12, 2002. Prior to the effective date of the Plan, Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc. formed Comdisco Holding Company,&nbsp;Inc., a Delaware corporation (the &#147;Company&#148; or &#147;Comdisco Holding&#148;). Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc. emerged as a wholly-owned subsidiary of Comdisco Holding. As a result, Comdisco Holding became the successor to Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc. A copy of the Plan for Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc., as well as other information related to distributions of cash and securities pursuant to the Plan can be found in a Current Report on Form&nbsp;8-K filed on August&nbsp;9, 2002 with the SEC by Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc. A copy of the Plan was filed as an exhibit thereto.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">General Terms of the Plan of Reorganization</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As more fully described in the Plan, the Company&#146;s business purpose is limited to the orderly sale or run-off of all of its remaining assets. Pursuant to the Plan and restrictions contained in its Certificate, the Company is specifically prohibited from engaging in any business activities inconsistent with its limited business purpose.&#160; Capitalized terms used but not defined in this section shall have the meanings as defined in the Plan.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In very general terms, the Plan contemplated six different classes of claims against the Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc. bankruptcy estate with the only remaining relevant classes of claims being described below:</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .75in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>&#147;Class&nbsp;C-4&#148; Claims. The largest class of claims against the Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc. bankruptcy estate, this class was comprised of general unsecured claims other than Class&nbsp;C-3 Claims and included holders of Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc. notes, bonds, credit lines and other trade debt (the &#147;C-4 creditors&#148;).</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .75in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>&#147;Class&nbsp;C-5A&#148; Claims. This class was comprised of equity claims, consisting of holders of shares of Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc. common stock and other &#147;Interests&#148; as defined in the Plan. All shares of common stock of Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc. were cancelled on August&nbsp;12, 2002 in accordance with the Plan.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Allowed Claims for Class&nbsp;C-5A received contingent distribution rights (&#147;CDRs&#148;) that entitle holders to share at increasing percentages in the proceeds realized from the monetization of the Company&#146;s assets based upon the present value of distributions made to the C-4 creditors in the bankruptcy estate of Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc. Information on the CDRs can be found in a Registration Statement on Form&nbsp;8-A filed by the Company on August&nbsp;12, 2002 with the SEC and in the section entitled &#147;Contingent Distribution Rights&#148; in Item 7, &#147;Management&#146;s Discussion and Analysis of Financial Condition and Results of Operations.&#148;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Pursuant to a Bankruptcy court order dated March&nbsp;27, 2003, approximately 4,388,000 CDRs were held by the Company&#146;s transfer agent and any distributions relating to these rights are held by the estate of Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc., pending resolution of the Class&nbsp;C-5A Claims related to the shares purchased pursuant to Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc.&#146;s Shared Investment Plan (the &#147;SIP&#148;). </font>Approximately 2,836,000 of the CDRs related to Class&nbsp;C-5A have been assigned to the Litigation Trust (as defined in the Plan) either in conjunction with settlements achieved with certain of the Federal or State SIP Defendants (as defined below), or turned over to the litigation trustee pursuant to an order entered by a Federal Court authorizing turnover of CDR assets.&#160; Approximately 868,000 CDRs were assigned to individuals or other trustees.&#160; Additionally, 92,000 CDRs related to Class&nbsp;C-5A Claims have been cancelled during the bankruptcy by the Company.&#160; The balance of approximately 592,000 CDRs are currently being held by the Company&#146;s transfer agent and any distributions relating to these rights are being held by the estate of Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In furtherance of the settlement evidenced by the Global Settlement Agreement (described in SIP Litigation) and as reported in the final report of the litigation trustee</font><font color="black" style="color:black;"> filed on October&nbsp;6, 2015 in the Bankruptcy court</font>, the Company will purchase from the litigation trustee approximately 3,000,000 CDRs and 26 shares of common stock acquired by the litigation trustee during the course of the SIP Litigation (the &#147;Assigned Assets&#148;). The Company will purchase the Assigned Assets at discounted prices of approximately $0.06898 per CDR and $4.33 per share of common stock, respectively. Shortly thereafter, the Company intends to cancel such acquired CDRs and shares of common stock.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">3<a name="PB_3_152729_5796"></a></p>
<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade align="left" style="color:#010101;"></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;"><a href="#TableOfContents" title="Click to go to Table of Contents">Table of Contents</a></font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Litigation Trust</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Plan provided that, under certain circumstances, subrogation rights that the Company may have against the SIP Participants (the &#147;SIP Participants&#148;) be placed in a trust for the benefit of C-4 creditors (the &#147;Trust Assets&#148;). Under the Plan, the Litigation Trust is solely responsible for collection of amounts due on the promissory notes of the SIP Participants who did not accept the SIP Relief (as defined in the Plan).</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In February&nbsp;1998, pursuant to the SIP, 106 SIP Participants took out full recourse, personal loans to purchase approximately six million shares of Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc.&#146;s common stock. In connection therewith, Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc. executed a guaranty dated February&nbsp;2, 1998 (the &#147;Guaranty&#148;) providing a guaranty of the loans in the event of default by the SIP Participants to the lenders under the SIP (the &#147;SIP Lenders&#148;).&#160; The Company and the SIP Lenders subsequently reached a settlement on the Guaranty that was approved by the Bankruptcy court on December&nbsp;9, 2004.&#160; </font><font color="black" style="color:black;">The Plan and the litigation trust agreement provided that, under certain circumstances, subrogation rights that the Company may have against the SIP Participants and their respective promissory notes be placed in a trust for the benefit of the C-4 creditors (the &#147;Trust Assets&#148;).&#160; Under the Plan, the Litigation Trust is solely responsible for collection of amounts due on the promissory notes of the sixty-nine SIP Participants who did not accept the SIP Relief (as defined in the Plan).&#160; The Company has a limited indemnification obligation to the litigation trustee under the litigation trust agreement.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">SIP Litigation:</font></b><font color="black" style="color:black;"> On February&nbsp;4, 2005, the Litigation Trust commenced lawsuits both in the United States District Court for the Northern District of Illinois (the &#147;Federal SIP Lawsuits&#148;) and in the Circuit Court of Cook County Illinois (the &#147;State SIP Lawsuits&#148;) to collect on&nbsp;the remaining&nbsp;SIP Participants&#146; promissory notes.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;">Federal SIP Lawsuits:</font></u><font color="black" style="color:black;"> The Litigation Trust filed and a federal district court judge entered summary judgments (and amended judgments) against all but one of the SIP Participants who were defendants in the federal cases (the &#147;Federal SIP Defendants&#148;) on their respective SIP promissory notes,&nbsp;and the Litigation Trust commenced collection actions against them.&nbsp;Additionally, the federal district court judge entered orders&nbsp;directing that certain CDRs and related proceeds held by the estate of Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc. and Computershare (f/k/a BNY Mellon) (holder of CDRs) on behalf of those Federal SIP Defendants be turned over to the Litigation Trust.&nbsp; Pursuant to such orders, the Company turned over CDRs and related proceeds and will continue to do so if additional orders are entered.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Following a series of motions, hearings and the completion of discovery</font>, at a hearing on July&nbsp;8, 2013, Judge Robert Gettleman set a trial date for September&nbsp;23, 2013.&#160; The trial&#146;s actual start date was September&nbsp;24, 2013 and the witness testimony and evidentiary phase was substantially completed on October&nbsp;10, 2013.&#160; On March&nbsp;27, 2014 the post-trial briefing was completed by the parties. The judge heard oral arguments on April&nbsp;16, 2014 and took the matter under advisement and would alert the parties when he came to either a partial or complete decision.&#160; On October&nbsp;21, 2014, the judge orally ruled and entered judgment in favor of the Federal SIP Defendants.&#160; The basis of the judge&#146;s ruling and judgment was his finding that both the bank and the Company committed an arranging violation under the applicable margin lending regulations.&#160; Therefore, the judge ruled that the promissory notes were void and unenforceable.&#160; <font color="black" style="color:black;">On October&nbsp;29, 2014, the litigation trustee filed an appeal of the judgment to the United States Court of Appeals for the Seventh Circuit.&nbsp; On November&nbsp;20, 2014, the Federal SIP Defendants filed a Notice of Appeal of the October&nbsp;21, 2014 judgment and of an order entered on August&nbsp;12, 2013.&#160; See update in &#147;Litigation Trust Reports and Settlement Update&#148; below.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:35.25pt;"><u><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;">State SIP Lawsuits:</font></u><font color="black" style="color:black;"> The Litigation Trust filed summary judgments against all of the SIP Participants who are defendants in the state cases (the &#147;State SIP Defendants&#148;, and, together with the Federal SIP Defendants, the &#147;SIP Defendants&#148;). Three of the State SIP Defendants filed Cross Motions for Summary Judgment.&nbsp; A hearing in the Circuit Court of Cook County on all of the summary judgment motions in the state cases was held on May&nbsp;12, 2010, and the judge granted the summary judgments in favor of the Litigation Trust and denied the various motions for summary judgments filed by the State SIP Defendants.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"><font style="font-size:10.0pt;">After a series of hearings, motions and counter-motions, amended pleadings and individual bankruptcies and settlements, the remaining </font><font color="black" style="color:black;">State SIP Defendants</font></font> and the litigation trustee entered into an agreed Stipulation And Order (the &#147;Stipulation&#148;) which, among other things, stays the trials in the state cases pending the resolution and any appeal of the trial in the federal&nbsp;cases.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;"><a href="#TableOfContents" title="Click to go to Table of Contents">Table of Contents</a></font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;">Litigation Trust Reports and Settlement Update:</font></u><font color="black" style="color:black;"> By early 2005,&nbsp;sixty-nine SIP Participant&#146;s promissory notes were transferred to the Litigation Trust.&nbsp;&nbsp;As reported in various Status Reports of Comdisco Litigation Trustee, of the sixty-nine SIP Participants:&#160; forty-one&nbsp;have settled or otherwise resolved their obligation; twelve have filed personal bankruptcy; and, sixteen&nbsp;notes remain outstanding (five in the federal court and eleven in the state court).</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;">On October&nbsp;1, 2015, the litigation trustee and the Company entered into a Global Settlement Agreement&nbsp;(the &#147;GSA&#148;) with the remaining SIP Defendants. Such settlement under the GSA does not have a material impact on the consolidated financial statements.&#160; </font><font color="black" style="color:black;">On October&nbsp;6, 2015, the&nbsp;litigation trustee filed with the United States Bankruptcy Court for the Northern District of Illinois Eastern Division a motion (the &#147;Motion&#148;) seeking the entry of an order to (i)&nbsp;approve a proposed settlement with the remaining federal and state defendants who had executed promissory notes in connection with Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc.&#146;s Shared Investment Plan, (ii)&nbsp;approve the filing of the final report of the litigation trustee and (iii)&nbsp;upon the wind down of the Comdisco Litigation Trust and final disbursement of its net proceeds to the beneficiaries, terminate the Comdisco Litigation Trust and discharge the litigation trustee and the Comdisco Litigation Trust Advisory Board. </font><font color="black" style="color:black;">&#160;On November&nbsp;23, 2015, a hearing was held in the Bankruptcy court and the judge granted an order approving the Motion and set a status hearing for April&nbsp;1, 2016.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For more details regarding the Litigation Trust and related proceedings, please refer to the Status Reports of Comdisco Litigation Trustee filed quarterly in the Bankruptcy court. Any proceeds collected by the Litigation Trust, net of expenses, will be considered Trust Assets and distributed in accordance with the Plan and the litigation trust agreement.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Changes in Governance</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On August&nbsp;12, 2004, Randolph I. Thornton became the sole director and officer of the Company and his appointment as Initial Disbursing Agent became effective. As Initial Disbursing Agent, Mr.&nbsp;Thornton assumed the roles and responsibilities performed by the former Board of Directors and officers of the Company, including all measures which are necessary to complete the administration of the reorganized debtors&#146; Plan and Chapter 11 cases.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On November&nbsp;16, 2015, Randolph I. Thornton renewed the appointment of the following employees, Robert E. T. Lackey, Deborah L. Dompke, Susan Long, Mary Ann Bolster and Michael J. Salerno, as Authorized Representatives of the Company. These individuals derive their authority from Mr.&nbsp;Thornton as sole director and officer of the Company, and report directly to him.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Filing of Certificate of Dissolution</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company filed on August&nbsp;12, 2004 a Certificate of Dissolution with the Secretary of State of the State of Delaware to formally extinguish Comdisco Holding Company,&nbsp;Inc.&#146;s corporate existence with the State of Delaware except for the purpose of completing the wind down contemplated by the Plan.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Narrative Description of Business</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">General</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Since emerging from Chapter 11 bankruptcy proceedings on August&nbsp;12, 2002, the Company has, pursuant to the Plan, focused on the monetization of its remaining assets. Therefore, comparisons of quarter-to-quarter or year-to-year results of operations should not be relied upon as an indication of the Company&#146;s future performance.&#160; Capitalized terms used but not defined in this section shall have the meanings as defined in the Plan.&#160; Under the Plan, the Company was charged with, and has been, liquidating its assets. While there have been no changes either to the Plan, or the Company&#146;s obligations under it, the Company adopted ASU 2013-07, <i>Liquidation Basis of Accounting </i>as of October&nbsp;1, 2014 and accordingly, determined that liquidation was imminent. Therefore, effective October&nbsp;1, 2014, the Company applied the liquidation basis of accounting on a prospective basis.</font> Pursuant to the Plan and restrictions contained in its Certificate, the Company is specifically prohibited from engaging in any business activities inconsistent with its limited business purpose. Since emerging from bankruptcy, the Company has not engaged in any new leasing or financing activities, except for previously existing customer commitments and to restructure existing equipment leases and loans to maximize the value of the Company&#146;s assets.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;"><a href="#TableOfContents" title="Click to go to Table of Contents">Table of Contents</a></font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Principal Business Location</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company&#146;s operations are primarily conducted through its principal office in Rosemont,&nbsp;Illinois which occupies leased short-term furnished executive office space.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Customers and Competition</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Due to the Company&#146;s limited business purpose, the Company is not dependent upon a single customer or group of customers to generate future investment or revenue opportunities. In addition, the Company&#146;s reorganization plan specifically prohibits the Company from engaging in any business activities inconsistent with its limited business purpose.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Employees</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On September&nbsp;30, 2015, the Company had five U.S. employees (one full-time and four part-time). No employees are represented by a labor union. The Company anticipates further reductions in its workforce as the wind down continues. </font>Three to four consultants periodically assist the Company on a consulting basis.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Other</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company does not own any patents, trademarks, licenses, franchises or concessions that it considers to be material to the Company&#146;s business.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company&#146;s business is not seasonal and due to the adoption of Liquidation Basis of Accounting, quarter-to-quarter results from operations are not applicable.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company&#146;s estimate of the fair value of its private company investments was made in consultation with Windspeed Acquisition Fund GP, LLC (&#147;Windspeed&#148;), a professional management group, who manages the Company&#146;s equity investments on an ongoing basis.&#160; Windspeed shares in the net receipts from the sale of the Company&#146;s equity investments at a set percentage in certain designated portions of the portfolio of companies.&#160; The Windspeed February&nbsp;2004 management agreement was extended on April&nbsp;5, 2011 (with an effective date of February&nbsp;21, 2011) until February&nbsp;20, 2013 (the &#147;Initial Extension&#148;).&#160; The Windspeed management agreement was subsequently extended effective February&nbsp;21, 2013 through February&nbsp;20, 2015 and extended again effective February&nbsp;12, 2015 through February&nbsp;12, 2017 (the &#147;Subsequent Extensions&#148;).&#160; Prior to the Initial Extension, Windspeed received fixed and declining management fees.&#160; Under the terms of the Initial and Subsequent Extensions, Windspeed is not, and will not, be paid any ongoing management fees.&#160; In lieu of such management fee payment, 100% of any proceeds from certain designated companies in the portfolio will go to Windspeed.&#160; Realized gains on the sale of equity investments are presented on a gross basis. Any management sharing amounts with Windspeed are included in accrued professional fees.&#160; The Company has received approximately $89,239,000 in proceeds (prior to management fees and sharing) since the inception of the management agreement with Windspeed.&#160; Windspeed has received a combined $15,444,000 in management fees and sharing through September&nbsp;30, 2015.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">During the quarter ended September&nbsp;30, 2014, it was announced that Ebates, one of the Company&#146;s private company Equity Investments, would be acquired by Rakuten,&nbsp;Inc. (&#147;Rakuten&#148;) a Japanese company.&#160; The Plan of Merger was signed on September&nbsp;24, 2014, pending various conditions, including regulatory approval.&#160; As of September&nbsp;30, 2014, the Company concluded that the offer price should be the primary input into the fair value measurement of Ebates.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On October&nbsp;9, 2014, Rakuten completed the acquisition and on October&nbsp;29, 2014, the Company received the initial distribution.&#160; The gross proceeds distributed were $17,720,000 of which the Company received $15,144,000 in net proceeds and Windspeed received $2,576,000 in management sharing pursuant to the management agreement.&#160; The remaining fair market value amount of approximately $1,911,000, before management sharing, is being held pursuant to the merger documents in an escrow until January&nbsp;2016.&#160; The actual amount to be distributed from the escrow may be impacted by provisions of, and claims asserted against, the escrow.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As a result of the adoption of liquidation basis of accounting, the Ebates transaction was assumed as of October&nbsp;1, 2014 and was included in the cumulative effect of an accounting change.&#160; As such, the net assets in</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">6<a name="PB_6_152807_7748"></a></p>

<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;"><a href="#TableOfContents" title="Click to go to Table of Contents">Table of Contents</a></font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">liquidation were increased $19,349,000 for the estimated net realizable value of equity investments.&#160; In addition, the CDR liability was increased by $6,101,000 primarily as a result of the Ebates transaction.</font>&#160; See Notes 3, 6 and 10 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements (in Liquidation), which are incorporated in this section by reference, for information about the Cumulative Effect of Accounting Change, Equity Investments and Fair Value Measurements, respectively.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Financial Information about Geographic Areas</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">See Note 2 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements (in Liquidation), which is incorporated in this section by reference.&#160; All of the company&#146;s assets and revenue are in North America.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">ITEM 1A. RISK FACTORS</font></b><a name="ITEM1A_RISKFACTORS_042017"></a></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The following risk factors and other information included in this Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K should be carefully considered. The risks and uncertainties described below are not the only ones the Company confronts. Additional risks and uncertainties not presently known to it or that it currently deems immaterial also may impair the Company&#146;s business operations and the implementation of the Plan. If any of the following risks actually occurs, the Company&#146;s business, financial condition, net assets in liquidation and the implementation of the Plan could be materially adversely affected.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Uncertainties Inherent in the CDR Liability Calculation</font></i></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The CDR liability is management&#146;s estimate of the amount of the remaining value of the Company to be shared by holders of CDRs at the sharing percentage of 37%. The net assets in liquidation which is used to calculate the CDR liability includes variables (e.g., estimated future operating costs and expenses, estimated future interest income, estimated other asset values,&nbsp;etc.) which are not under the control of the Company. Such variables are inherently uncertain due to the impact of influences such as time, inflation or deflation, interest rate changes, third party credit risks, domestic events, court or tax rulings contrary to the Company&#146;s expectations, timing and amounts of distributions to C-4 creditors by the Litigation Trust, and matters that could impact the timing on the wind down of the Company.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Impact of Recoveries by Litigation Trust on the Company&#146;s Obligation to Make Payments in Respect of Contingent Distribution Rights</font></i></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:40.5pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As the present value of distributions to certain C-4 creditors has reached the 100% threshold level of percentage recovery established pursuant to the Plan, holders of CDRs are entitled to receive payments from the Company equal to 37% of each dollar available to be distributed to Comdisco C-4 creditors in accordance with the Plan. All payments by the Company in respect of CDRs are made from the Company&#146;s available cash-on-hand and not from funds distributed by the Litigation Trust. The Company expects to maintain cash reserves sufficient to make any required payments pursuant to its CDR liability arising from either the Company&#146;s net assets in liquidation or any net distributions from the Litigation Trust to the C-4 creditors.&#160; Any actual net distributions by the Litigation Trust to the C-4 creditors will increase the Company&#146;s liability to CDR holders.&#160; Estimates of such net distributions are currently based on the likely anticipated distribution reported by the litigation trustee in its supplement to the final report filed in the U.S. Bankruptcy Court and any such liability is reflected on the financial statements under Liabilities at Supplemental CDR Liability Due To Anticipated Litigation Trust Distribution.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;"><b><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Final Tax Clearances</font></i></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The ability of the Company to effectuate timely assessments and receive final tax liabilities, if any, from the applicable state and federal taxing authorities to allow for the closure of the bankruptcy estate.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Uncertainties Inherent in the Determination of Value of the Ebates Escrow</font></i></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The determination of the value of the Ebates escrow is management&#146;s estimate of such value at a moment in time based on information available to management at that time. The estimate of value is inherently uncertain due to factors that could impact the payout from the Ebates escrow. Some of the factors that could impact the timing and amount of the projections are claims and legal expenses assessed against the Ebates escrow.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">7<a name="PB_7_152822_141"></a></p>
<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade align="left" style="color:#010101;"></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;"><a href="#TableOfContents" title="Click to go to Table of Contents">Table of Contents</a></font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;"><b><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">The Payment of Dividends and Distributions</font></i></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">All funds generated from the Company&#146;s remaining assets are required by the Plan to be used to satisfy liabilities of the Company and, to the extent funds are available, to pay dividends on the Company&#146;s Common Stock and to make distributions with respect to the CDRs in the manner and priorities set forth in the Plan. Because of the composition and nature of its remaining assets, the Company expects to generate funds from the sale or run-off of its remaining assets at a decreasing rate over time. The Company has material restrictions on its ability, and does not expect or intend, to make any significant investments in new or additional assets. Accordingly, the amount of funds potentially available to pay dividends on the Company&#146;s Common Stock and to make distributions with respect to the CDRs is limited to the Company&#146;s Net Assets in Liquidation.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Uncertainties in Collections and Recoveries</font></i></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company believes that its collections and recoveries on accounts previously written off could provide future but diminishing cash flows.&#160; The amount and timing of such collections and recoveries are dependent upon many factors including any offsets or counterclaims that may be asserted against the Company and the ability of a former lessee or debtor or its respective estate to pay the claim or any portion thereof.&#160; Some of these factors are beyond the control of the Company.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;"><b><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Uncertainties Relating to the Bankruptcy Plan and the Limited Business Plan and Impact of the Adoption of Liquidation Basis of Accounting</font></i></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company believes the most critical judgment areas in the application of its accounting policies are the estimated future cash inflows and future outflows.&#160; As of October&nbsp;1, 2014, the Company has adopted the liquidation basis of accounting on a prospective basis which requires the estimation of and accrual of all projected future cash inflows and future outflows associated with implementing and completing the plan of liquidation and requires management to make estimates that affect the amounts reported in the consolidated statements of net assets in liquidation and the related notes. Results could differ from these estimates and may affect the net assets in liquidation and actual cash flows.&#160; These estimates could be affected by the timing of the wind down of the estate, adverse tax ruling or changes, adverse court rulings and external events beyond the control of the Company.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;"><b><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">The Company&#146;s Liquidity is Dependent on Cash on Hand</font></i></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company&#146;s liquidity depends on cash on hand.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;"><b><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Limited Public Market for Common Stock</font></i></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">There is currently a limited public market for the Company&#146;s Common Stock. Holders of the Company&#146;s Common Stock may, therefore, have difficulty selling their Common Stock, should they decide to do so. In addition, there can be no assurances that such markets will continue or that any shares of Common Stock which may be purchased could be sold without incurring a loss. Any such market price of the Common Stock may not necessarily bear any relationship to the Company&#146;s net assets in liquidation value or any other established criteria of value, and may not be indicative of the market price for the Common Stock in the future. Further, the market price of the Common Stock may be volatile depending on a number of factors, including the status of the Company&#146;s business performance, its limited business purpose, industry dynamics, news announcements or changes in general economic conditions.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;"><b><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Limited Public Market for Contingent Distribution Rights</font></i></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">There is currently a limited public market for the Company&#146;s CDRs. Holders of the Company&#146;s CDRs may, therefore, have difficulty selling their CDRs, should they decide to do so. In addition, there can be no assurances that such markets will continue or that any CDRs which may be purchased could be sold without incurring a loss. Any such market price of the CDRs may not necessarily bear any relationship to the Company&#146;s net assets in liquidation value, assets, past operating results, financial condition or any other established criteria of value, and may not be indicative of the market price for the CDRs in the future. Further, the market price of the CDRs may be volatile</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">8<a name="PB_8_152849_7608"></a></p>

<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;"><a href="#TableOfContents" title="Click to go to Table of Contents">Table of Contents</a></font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">depending on a number of factors, including the status of the Company&#146;s business performance, industry dynamics, news announcements or changes in general economic conditions.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;"><b><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Uncertainties Relating to the Wind Down of Operations</font></i></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company has reduced the size and complexity of its organizational and systems infrastructure concurrently with the monetization of its assets. The success of the Company&#146;s continuing wind down of operations and implementation of the Order entered by the Bankruptcy court authorizing the organizational systems infrastructure wind down is dependent upon the ability of the Company to effectively maintain its operations with limited personnel.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:1.0in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company is currently projecting December&nbsp;31, 2016 as the end date for its wind down of operations. It is anticipated that by this date the Company will have, among other things: finalized the settlement of the SIP, received the projected escrow funds from the Ebates transaction, reduced all of its assets to cash, resolved its final federal and state tax obligations, determined its final CDR liability (which will include the impact of the actual distribution by the Litigation Trust to the C-4 creditors), made distributions of all available cash to holders of its common stock and CDRs in the manner and priorities set forth in the Plan, cancelled such common stock and CDRs and completed all regulatory filings.&#160; Accordingly, it has made appropriate expense accruals for such time period in its calculation of Net Assets in Liquidation. However, the projected remaining wind down period could be either shortened or lengthened by other intervening matters not currently known to management.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;"><b><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Impact of Interest Rates</font></i></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Changes in interest rates could impact the value of certain of the Company&#146;s assets.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">ITEM 1B. UNRESOLVED STAFF COMMENTS</font></b><a name="ITEM1B_UNRESOLVEDSTAFFCOMMENTS_042024"></a></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Not applicable.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">ITEM 2. PROPERTIES</font></b><a name="ITEM2_PROPERTIES_042032"></a></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Since October&nbsp;31, 2004, the Company has leased short-term furnished executive office space for all of its operations at 5600 N. River Road in Rosemont,&nbsp;Illinois. The terms of its rental agreement provide the Company with the ability to match its actual leased space with its declining space requirements.&#160; The Company does not own any property.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">ITEM 3. LEGAL PROCEEDINGS</font></b><a name="ITEM3_LEGALPROCEEDINGS_042034"></a></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Bankruptcy Proceeding</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company continues to appear before the Bankruptcy court from time to time to clarify and administer matters related to the Plan and the wind down of the operations of the Company. <font color="black" style="color:black;">&#160;On June&nbsp;28, 2011, the bankruptcy case of Comdisco,&nbsp;Inc., case no. 01-24795, was reassigned from Judge Bruce Black to Judge Jack&nbsp;Schmetterer.</font></font><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:black;"> On November&nbsp;23, 2015, a hearing was held in the Bankruptcy court and the judge granted an order approving the Motion and set a hearing for April&nbsp;1, 2016.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Litigation Trust Ongoing Litigation</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;">The Plan and the litigation trust agreement provided that, under certain circumstances, subrogation rights that the Company may have against the SIP Participants and their respective promissory notes be placed in a trust for the benefit of the C-4 creditors (the &#147;Trust Assets&#148;).&#160; Under the Plan, the Litigation Trust is solely responsible for collection of amounts due on the promissory notes of the SIP Participants who did not accept the SIP Relief (as defined in the Plan).&#160; The Company has a limited indemnification obligation to the litigation trustee under the litigation trust agreement.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">9<a name="PB_9_152909_8146"></a></p>
